## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves predicting the rate of change of concentration dA_dt in a chemical reaction, which is a classic ordinary differential equation problem in chemical kinetics. The rate typically depends on the reactant concentration A and possibly on time t if external factors (e.g., catalyst deactivation, temperature ramps) are present.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order decay: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, e.g., surfaceŌĆælimited reaction or photolysis under constant light)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A (simple exponential decay, unimolecular reaction)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of two identical molecules)
- n-th order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general powerŌĆælaw kinetics, c1 is the reaction order)
- Mixed-order polynomial: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (parallel first- and second-order pathways)
- Autocatalytic with product: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (rate depends on both reactant and product, typical of autocatalysis or logisticŌĆætype depletion)
- Generalized autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * (c2 - A)**c3 (complex nucleationŌĆægrowth or activationŌĆædeactivation mechanisms)
- Time-dependent rate exponential: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (rate constant changes exponentially, e.g., catalyst deactivation or thermal ramping)
- Time-power rate: dA_dt = c0 * t**c1 * A (powerŌĆælaw time dependence of the rate constant, e.g., diffusionŌĆælimited aging)
- Time-only forcing: dA_dt = c0 * t**c1 (rate independent of A, e.g., external supply or injection)
- Linear time forcing: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * t (rate increasing/decreasing linearly with time)
- Sum of power and time: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * t (first-order reaction plus externally controlled source/sink)
- Exponential dependence on A: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * A) (strong positive feedback, e.g., thermal runaway or explosion)
- Log-time dependence: dA_dt = c0 * log(c1 + t) (gradual acceleration of rate, e.g., in some dissolution processes)
- Rational time-concentration: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + t) (rate decays hyperbolically with time due to e.g., catalyst consumption)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Power-law rate dA/dt ŌłØ A^c implies the reaction is of order c; fractional orders indicate complex or chain mechanisms.
- Sigmoidal rate shape dA/dt ŌłØ A*(c-A) gives an inflection point in A(t) and suggests autocatalysis or product-promoted reaction.
- Explicit time factors multiplying A (e.g., exp(c*t)*A) represent time-varying rate constants, often due to catalyst deactivation or changing temperature.
- Additive combinations of different A powers (e.g., A + A^2) indicate parallel elementary steps contributing to the overall rate.
- Rate independent of A (only t functions) points to zero-order kinetics, usually caused by surface saturation, constant irradiation, or external supply limitation.
- A negative exponent (c1<0) in A^c1 means rate decreases as A increases, hinting at substrate inhibition or product inhibition.
- The curvature of dA/dt vs A reveals reaction order: linear for first-order, concave up for >1st order, concave down for fractional <1st order.
- Vanishing rate at a non-zero A (e.g., A = c1) signals equilibrium, complete consumption of a limiting species, or reversible step.
- Exponential dependence on A (exp(c*A)) implies strong positive feedback that can lead to ignition or runaway reactions.
- Time t appearing without A often serves as a proxy for an unmeasured process (mixing, heating, light intensity ramp) affecting the rate.

c5)", "A*c0 + A*c1 + c2 + c3*sin(c4*log(A*c5 + 1) + c6)", "A*c0 + c1*sin(c2*log(A*c3 + 1) + c4)", "A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2 + c3*log(A*c4 + 1) + c5*sin(c6*log(A*c7 + 1) + c8)", "A*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*log(A*c4 + 1) + c5*sin(c6*log(A*c7 + c8*t + 1) + c9)"]

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: -0.15727681835797813*A + 0.49113636468363491*sin(log(A + 1))**

Note that `_t = 3.122751145472426` is a fixed constant, so `c1*_t = 0.15727681835797813 * 3.122751145472426 Ōēł 0.49113636468363491`.

The GT is: `c_A * A + c_s * sin(log(A + 1))` where `c_A Ōēł -0.15728` and `c_s Ōēł 0.49114`.

Key features of GT:
1. Linear term in A
2. sin(log(A + 1)) term
3. **No dependence on t** (since _t is a fixed constant absorbed into c1)
4. No other basis functions

Let me analyze each candidate, checking if it can reduce to `╬▒*A + ╬▓*sin(log(A+1))` for some constants.

For candidates with terms involving `t`: these can only match if the `t`-dependent terms can be zeroed out by setting their coefficients to 0.

For candidates with `sin(c*log(A*c+1) + c)`: this matches sin(log(A+1)) when the multiplier inside log is 1, the coefficient of log is 1, and the phase shift is 0.

For candidates with `cos(c*log(A*c+1))`: cos can equal sin with a phase shift of ŽĆ/2, so `cos(log(A+1)) = sin(log(A+1) + ŽĆ/2)`, but we need `sin(log(A+1))` without phase shift. Actually, `c*cos(c*log(A*c+1))` with appropriate constants: we can write `cos(x) = sin(x + ŽĆ/2)`, but the GT has `sin(log(A+1))` with no phase shift. So `cos(log(A+1)) ŌēĀ sin(log(A+1))`. However, if the candidate has `c7*cos(c8*log(A*c9+1))`, this equals `c7*sin(c8*log(A*c9+1) + ŽĆ/2)`, which is `sin(log(A+1))` only if the phase is 0 mod 2ŽĆ, but cos always introduces ŽĆ/2 phase. So cos alone cannot match sin(log(A+1)) unless there's a separate phase parameter.

Let me systematically go through candidates that have the right structure:

**Candidates with `A*c + c*log(A*c+1) + c*sin(c*log(A*c+1) + c)` structure:**

These can match if we set the log coefficient to 0 and the sin term appropriately.

**Candidate 28:** `A*c0 + c1*log(A*c2 + 1) + c3*sin(c4*log(A*c5 + 1) + c6)`
Set c1=0, c4=1, c5=1, c6=0. Then: `c0*A + c3*sin(log(A+1))`. Ō£ō
